# Fine-Tuning for LLMs: from Beginner to Advanced

> This course capitalizes on the latest advancements in Large Language Models (LLMs) like FLAN-T5, enabling professionals to harness these tools effectively in the rapidly-evolving AI landscape. Instructor Axel Sirota helps you establish a strong foundation in the basics of LLMs, exploring their architecture, evolution, and role in the current AI landscape. Delve into prompt engineering and learn ho

### 2. 1. Introduction to Large Language Models (LLMs)

#### LLMs: Revolutionizing AI

>

#### The architecture of LLMs
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Now let's unpack the structure and inner workings of large language models, or LLMs, focusing on the revolutionary transformer architecture.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=15)** Imagine understanding the intricate design of a highly efficient modern kitchen.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=22)** That's what we are doing with LLMs today.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=27)** Transformers introduced by researchers at Google in 2017 are the backbone of most modern LLMs.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=37)** They have radically changed how machines process language.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=43)** At their core, transformers consist of layers of encoders and decoders.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=50)** The encoders read and process the input text while the decoders generate output based on that information.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=61)** Think of encoders as the kitchen staff who prepare all your ingredients, and decoders as the chefs who put those ingredients together to create a dish.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=74)** It is extremely important to not focus on each box and what does it mean.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=81)** We will get to that.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=82)** For now get the big picture of an encoder and a decoder.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=88)** One of the key innovations in transformers is the self-attention mechanism.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=94)** This allows the model to weight the importance of different words relative to others in a sentence.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=103)** For example, in the sentence, "The chef who trained me cooks well," the model would recognize that chef and cooks are crucially linked despite the distance between them.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=121)** This understanding improves the model's ability to handle nuances in language.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=129)** Unlike older models such as RNNs or LSTMs which process data sequentially, transformers process all parts of the data simultaneously.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=144)** This parallel processing is akin to multiple kitchen stations working at the same time dramatically speeding up tasks.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=154)** Now let's test your understanding.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=158)** How does the self-attention mechanism enhance the transformer's ability to understand context within sentences?
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=168)** Think about it for 30 seconds.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=172)** LLMs use these transformer architectures to excel at tasks like translation, content creation, and more by effectively understanding and generating human-like text, Their ability to quickly process vast amounts of data and grasp complex patterns makes them invaluable across different fields.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=207)** To dive a bit deeper, each layer of a transformer can be thought as a mini brain, each making its own decisions about which parts of the text are important.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/the-architecture-of-llms?u=76281980&t=220)** These layers stack together forming a powerful network that fine tunes language and generation.

#### Applications of LLMs
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/applications-of-llms?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/applications-of-llms?u=76281980&t=0)** - So we know a bit about the architecture behind LLMs.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/applications-of-llms?u=76281980&t=3)** Now let's explore their transformative applications across various sectors.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/applications-of-llms?u=76281980&t=10)** As we go through these examples, think of LLMs as the master chefs of data transforming raw information into delightful, insightful experiences.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/applications-of-llms?u=76281980&t=22)** In healthcare, LLMs are making significant strides.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/applications-of-llms?u=76281980&t=27)** For instance, they assist in cancer care by providing support in diagnostics and patient management.
>

#### Comparing LLMs

>

>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=17)** Let's equip you with the knowledge to select the right model for your tasks and into choosing the perfect tool for a gourmet dish.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=30)** First up, encoder-only models, such as BERT.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=36)** These models focus on analyzing and understanding input data.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=43)** BERT is trained on tasks like masked language modeling, where it learns to predict missing words in a sentence.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=53)** This training helps the model grasp context from both directions, left to right and right to left, much like a sous chef needs to understand all ingredients and their interactions.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=70)** BERT and its variants are extensively used for tasks where understanding text is crucial, such as sentiment analysis or question answering.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=84)** It's like having a food critic who specializes in dissecting and understanding the flavors within a dish.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=94)** Next, decoder-only models, like OpenAI's GPT series.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=99)** These models excel in generating text based on the input they receive.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=107)** GPT-3, for example, uses an approach called autoregressive language modeling, where it predicts the next word in a sequence, learning from each word it has predicted.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=123)** Imagine a chef who dishes out course after course, each influenced by the last GPT-3 is a powerhouse in applications requiring content creation, from writing articles to composting emails.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=143)** It's akin to an innovative chef who creates new recipes based on a few given ingredients.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=152)** Moving to encoder-decoder models, which combine the functionalities of the first two, T5, or Text-to-Text Transfer Transformer, exemplifies this architecture.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=167)** It is trained on a text-to-text basis, where every task, be it translation, classification, or summarization, is converted into a text generation problem.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=181)** This tool capability allows us to understand and generate text, akin to a chef who both plans the menu and cooks the meal.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=194)** T5 and similar models are versatile, suited for a range of applications across different languages and tasks, making them Swiss army knives of the LLM world.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=208)** Consider Meta's Llama 3 8B, an 8-billion parameter model.

> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=216)** Hosting such a model for tasks like prompt engineering requires substantial computational resources.

>

>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=248)** This emphasizes the need to consider the model size when matching a model to our budget and infrastructure capabilities.
>
> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=261)** However, techniques like model distillation and quantization can reduce the computational load, making it feasible to deploy these powerful models in production environments.

> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=294)** To select the best LLM for your task, start by considering the nature of the task.
>
> **[5:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=300)** Is it understanding, generating, or both?
>
> **[5:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=305)** If your focus is on understanding or analyzing text, encoder-only models may suffice.
>
> **[5:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=314)** For content generation, decoder-only models are preferable.

>
> **[5:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=334)** For nuanced tasks specific to your data, fine-tuning might be essential.
>
> **[5:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=342)** Building an LLM from scratch can be as costly as establishing a high-end restaurant.
>
> **[5:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=349)** It requires substantial investment in computational resources, data, and expertise.
>
> **[5:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/comparing-llms?u=76281980&t=358)** Therefore, leveraging existing models and focusing on fine-tuning or prompt engineering is often more practical.

>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/flan-t5-in-focus?u=76281980&t=9)** We are going to unpack the architecture of FLAN-T5 and show how versatile this model can be across a variety of tasks.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/flan-t5-in-focus?u=76281980&t=18)** Think of FLAN-T5 as a highly skilled chef who not only excels in creating a wide array of dishes, but also adapts recipes to new constraints effortlessly.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/flan-t5-in-focus?u=76281980&t=32)** FLAN-T5, or Factual Language Annotation T5, builds on the T5 model or Text-to-text Transfer Transformer model.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/flan-t5-in-focus?u=76281980&t=44)** The original T5 model converts all NLP tasks into a unified text-to-text format where inputs and outputs are treated as text strings.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/flan-t5-in-focus?u=76281980&t=55)** This includes everything from translation and summarization to question answering.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/flan-t5-in-focus?u=76281980&t=62)** FLAN-T5 enhances T5 by training it with a technique called instruction tuning.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/flan-t5-in-focus?u=76281980&t=70)** Rather than training on a specific task format data sets, FLAN-T5 uses a diverse set of prompts or instructions during its training phase.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/flan-t5-in-focus?u=76281980&t=81)** Let it be translate, Q&A, summarization, or even more.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/flan-t5-in-focus?u=76281980&t=87)** This method trains the model to better understand and generate responses based on natural language instructions, broadening its ability to handle tasks it wasn't explicitly trained on.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/flan-t5-in-focus?u=76281980&t=105)** To utilize FLAN-T5, you simply frame your task as a natural language instruction.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/flan-t5-in-focus?u=76281980&t=112)** For instance, if you need a summary of a text, you might input, "Summarize the following article."
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/flan-t5-in-focus?u=76281980&t=121)** If you're looking for translation, your prompt could be, "Translate the following text from English to French."
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/flan-t5-in-focus?u=76281980&t=129)** This flexibility makes FLAN-T5 incredibly powerful in real world applications where tasks can vary significantly.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/flan-t5-in-focus?u=76281980&t=139)** FLAN-T5's ability to interpret and execute a wide range of instructions makes it akin to a digital Swiss Army knife.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/flan-t5-in-focus?u=76281980&t=149)** Its versatility comes from the model's foundational training, which enables it to adapt instructions across context without needing retraining for each specific task.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/flan-t5-in-focus?u=76281980&t=164)** Integrating FLAN-T5 into applications is straightforward thanks to frameworks like high phase transformers library, where FLAN-T5 models are readily available.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/flan-t5-in-focus?u=76281980&t=177)** This accessibility allows developers to deploy powerful NLP tools quickly and efficiently, enhancing user interaction and data processing capabilities to get our answer.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/flan-t5-in-focus?u=76281980&t=193)** And finally, to get our action.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/flan-t5-in-focus?u=76281980&t=198)** As we continue to explore the capabilities of different LLMs, keep in mind the unique strengths of models like FLAN-T5.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/flan-t5-in-focus?u=76281980&t=207)** Stay tuned for our next segment, where we dive deeper into how these technologies can be tailored to meet specific needs in more specialized fields.

### 3. 2. Utilizing LLMs with Prompt Engineering

#### Basics of prompt engineering
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/basics-of-prompt-engineering?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/basics-of-prompt-engineering?u=76281980&t=0)** - Welcome to our session on the basics of prompt engineering, a crucial skill for anyone working with large language models or LLMs.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/basics-of-prompt-engineering?u=76281980&t=11)** Today, we'll break down what prompt engineering is, the key components of a prompt, and how you can effectively interact with LLMs in various environments.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/basics-of-prompt-engineering?u=76281980&t=22)** Imagine being a director in a play where your actors are AI models, and your script is the prompt.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/basics-of-prompt-engineering?u=76281980&t=31)** The better your script, the better the performance.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/basics-of-prompt-engineering?u=76281980&t=35)** Let's start by defining a prompt.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/basics-of-prompt-engineering?u=76281980&t=39)** A prompt is essentially an instruction or a set of instructions you give to an LLM.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/basics-of-prompt-engineering?u=76281980&t=48)** It sets the stage for how the model should respond.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/basics-of-prompt-engineering?u=76281980&t=53)** Think of it as giving context or a backstory before asking a question.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/basics-of-prompt-engineering?u=76281980&t=60)** This context helps the model understand not just what you're asking, but also how to tailor each response appropriately.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/basics-of-prompt-engineering?u=76281980&t=73)** Interacting with LLMs can happen in several ways depending on your setup and needs.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/basics-of-prompt-engineering?u=76281980&t=80)** First, we have applications, which are user-friendly and often require minimal coding skills.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/basics-of-prompt-engineering?u=76281980&t=90)** These are great for everyday users.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/basics-of-prompt-engineering?u=76281980&t=95)** Next, we have web interfaces, which are similar, but tend to offer more flexibility, and are accessible from any device with internet access.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/basics-of-prompt-engineering?u=76281980&t=108)** These platforms are perfect for those who might need to access the model on the go.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/basics-of-prompt-engineering?u=76281980&t=115)** Lastly, for developers, interacting directly through code offers the most control.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/basics-of-prompt-engineering?u=76281980&t=123)** This method involves writing scripts that sends prompts to the model, process the responses, and integrate them into larger applications or services.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/basics-of-prompt-engineering?u=76281980&t=138)** Prompt engineering is not just about asking questions, it's about asking the right questions in the right way.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/basics-of-prompt-engineering?u=76281980&t=149)** By mastering this, you can dramatically enhance the functionality and utility of LLMs across various applications.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/basics-of-prompt-engineering?u=76281980&t=159)** Experiment with different prompts, tweak your context, and see how your model's responses change.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/basics-of-prompt-engineering?u=76281980&t=168)** It's like fine tuning a recipe until you get the perfect flavor.

#### Crafting effective prompts
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Let's uncover common patterns for prompt design and key aspects to consider, ensuring your interactions with these AI models are both efficient and productive.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=14)** Think of prompt engineering as crafting a key that unlocks the full potential of a sophisticated AI brain.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=23)** Prompt design is crucial because it directly influences the quality and relevance of the responses you receive from an LLM.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=35)** A well-designed prompt should be clear, concise, and specific.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=42)** It should provide enough context to guide the model's response, but not so much that it overwhelms it or confuses the model.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=53)** Some models, especially smaller ones like T5, have specific prompt patterns that are optimized for their training.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=64)** For instance, T5 transforms every task into text-to-text format, often starting with a keyword that signals the task type, such as translate, summarize, or question for question answering.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=81)** This standardized approach helps the model quickly recognize a task and apply the appropriate process and strategy.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=91)** Now that we know the basics, let's dive into the three main patterns for prompt engineering that can help you maximize the efficiency of your interactions with LLMs: the few-shot pattern, the cognitive verifier pattern, and the question refinement pattern.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=111)** First is the few-shot pattern.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=114)** This involves providing several examples of the task at hand before presenting the model with a new instance to solve.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=124)** For example, if you're teaching the model to identify animal names in text, you might give examples with labeled animals before asking it to identify animals in a new sentence.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=139)** For example, given the prompt: "The quick brown fox jumps over the lazy dog," we set identify as fox and dog.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=154)** Then, we add the real prompt: "A sheep and a wolf became unlikely friends."
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=163)** When we ask to identify the animal, the LLM will have much more information about the format of the output.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=173)** Next, we have the cognitive verifier pattern, which is extremely useful when you need a right approach to a subject and aren't sure whether we are tackling all of its angles.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=187)** By using this pattern, the LLM increases the reliability of the outputs by checking the information needed before the final response.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=198)** It is really useful when it is critical to have reliable and faithful information in order to solve a problem.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=207)** For example, the common prompt that starts the conversation should be: Whenever I ask a question, only ask me for additional information to clarify what I'm asking before providing a final answer.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=224)** Please combine all my responses.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=229)** Such a prompt will trigger a set of questions to further refine what are we looking for.
>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=238)** I encourage you to try it out in your best chatbot of your choosing.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=246)** Finally, the question refinement pattern is used to get the LLM to refine or clarify a question before answering it.
>
> **[4:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=256)** The LLM asks additional questions to get more information or context, which it then uses to provide a more accurate or relevant answer.
>
> **[4:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=268)** The initial prompt of such a chat would be: Whenever I ask a question, ask me additional questions to clarify what I'm asking before you provide an answer.
>
> **[4:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=283)** As you experiment with these patterns, you'll find that the way you phrase a prompt can dramatically alter the outcomes you achieve with an LLM.
>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/crafting-effective-prompts?u=76281980&t=294)** Test different approaches, refine your prompts based on the responses, and continuously learn from their interactions.

#### Demo: Prompt engineering with FLAN-T5
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-prompt-engineering-with-flan-t5?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-prompt-engineering-with-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Okay, welcome everybody to the first demo of this course.

> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-prompt-engineering-with-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=5)** All of the demos in this course are going to be using Google Colaboratory.

> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-prompt-engineering-with-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=13)** Google Colab, for short, is a platform where we can put our notebook files, and it will connect us for free to an instance in Google Cloud platform where we can also connect a GPU.
>

So we say few-shots and in context learning, they are almost the same, so we call it in context learning when we are providing like some kind of question answering scheme.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-using-icl-and-patterns-while-prompting?u=76281980&t=262)** It's a historical term more than a difference in technicalities.
>
> **[4:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-using-icl-and-patterns-while-prompting?u=76281980&t=268)** The idea is the same.

>
> **[4:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-using-icl-and-patterns-while-prompting?u=76281980&t=278)** Then another context, another question, another answer.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-using-icl-and-patterns-while-prompting?u=76281980&t=282)** Finally, we are going to provide a new context like "Mount Everest is the highest mountain in the world" and we ask what is the highest mountain in the world?
>
> **[4:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-using-icl-and-patterns-while-prompting?u=76281980&t=292)** We combine, tokenize, generate, decode, and what we get back is Mount Everest.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-using-icl-and-patterns-while-prompting?u=76281980&t=302)** So we can see that this few-shot pattern of providing examples is an extremely good idea to improve your prompting to LLMs that are not particularly designed for any type of input, like for example, GPT4, but are small and can be used for specific tasks for applications, chat bots, or even for augmenting productivity.

### 4. 3. Transfer Learning for NLP Tasks

#### Transfer learning in LLMs
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980&t=0)** - Let's dive into the fascinating world of machine learning techniques, focusing on transfer learning and fine-tuning within large language models.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980&t=11)** We'll start by introducing these concepts with an analogy, then explore how they are applied in AI, and understand when to use each method effectively.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980&t=24)** Imagine you're a chef trying to make a variety of dishes.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980&t=28)** If you move to a new restaurant, you don't need to relearn everything about cooking.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980&t=33)** Instead, you adapt your skills to the new kitchen and menu.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980&t=39)** This adaptation is similar to transfer learning, where a model developed for one task is tweaked to handle a related but slightly different task.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980&t=51)** In contrast, imagine a chef who not only moves to a new restaurant, but also learns to cook an entirely new cuisine.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980&t=60)** These would require more in-depth training and practice akin to fine-tuning, where an existing model is extensively trained on a new, often significantly different data.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980&t=76)** Technically, transfer learning in the context of AI involves taking a model that's been pre-trained on a large data set, and adapting it to a specialized task with only minor modifications.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980&t=91)** This is often done by adding a new component or head to the model that is specifically trained on the new task, while keeping most of the regional model's structure intact.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980&t=105)** For instance, a pre-trained language model might get a new output layer to classify email sentiments, where only this new layer learns from the emails, while the rest of the model remains unchanged.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980&t=120)** Fine-tuning, however, involves adjusting the entire model and a new dataset.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980&t=126)** Here, all the weights and biases in the model are updated through a further training.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980&t=133)** This approach is more resource intensive, but necessary when a new task differs significantly from those where the model was originally trained on.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980&t=145)** While transfer learning might be likened to a quick course update for a chef, fine-tuning is more like undergoing an entire culinary school program again.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980&t=157)** Fine-tuning a model on a specialized task like legal documents analysis might require significant computation and data, reflecting in higher costs and longer development times.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980&t=170)** Choosing between transfer learning and fine-tuning depends on your specific needs.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980&t=175)** Transfer learning is ideal when the tasks are similar enough, and resources are limited, as it allows for quicker adaptations with less data.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980&t=185)** Fine-tuning is best when the tasks are very different or when maximum accuracy is critical, despite the higher costs and longer timeframes involved.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980&t=198)** In this exploration, we've seen how transfer learning and fine-tuning play pivotal roles in deploying LMS efficiently.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/transfer-learning-in-llms?u=76281980&t=207)** By understanding these techniques, you can better strategize your model development to meet your specific needs, ensuring optimal performance and resource management.

> **Analogies:** imagine (2), similar to (1), for instance (1)
> **CLI Commands:** make (1)
> **Env Vars:** lms (1)
> **Speakers:** - let (1)

#### Choosing models for transfer learning
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] So we know what transfer learning is.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=4)** Now let's explore how to choose the best models for transfer learning, especially when dealing with scarce datasets.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=13)** We look at three specific examples, including the classic pneumonia detection task using VGG-19.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=22)** Choosing the right model for transfer learning involves considering several factors.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=28)** The key criteria include the similarity of the source and target tasks, the size and quality of the pre-trained model, and the compatibility with your specific requirements.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=43)** First, let's examine a healthcare scenario detecting pneumonia from chest X-rays.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=50)** This is a classic example where transfer learning shines due to the scarcity of annotated medical images.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=61)** VGG-19 is a deep convolutional neural network that has been pre-trained on the ImageNet dataset, which contains millions of labeled images across a thousand categories.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=75)** Although these categories are diverse, the low-level features that VGG-19 learns, such as edges and textures, are transferable to medical imaging tasks.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=89)** Here, what we do is we are going to add a new Dense layer on top of the VGG-19 base to classify X-ray images into pneumonia or non-pneumonia categories.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=104)** Freezing the base layers ensures that the pre-trained weights are retained, making the model effective even with a small dataset.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=115)** Notice that first we download the base_model, and then what we're going to do is flatten the output and add a simple Dense layer on top of it.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=128)** Finally, we do our final Dense classification layer.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=134)** We create the model and set the base_model as non trainable.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=141)** We compile with the classic parameters for these types of models, and that's it.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=149)** This model will learn from the pneumonia dataset how to classify pneumonia, even if VGG-19 never ever saw an X-ray scan in its whole life.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=161)** Now, let's consider sentiment analysis on a limited dataset of product reviews.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=168)** For this task, BERT is a powerful model.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=173)** BERT has been pre-trained on a large corpus of text and is highly effective at understanding the nuances of language.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=182)** This makes it ideal for tasks like sentiment analysis, where context and subtleties in text are crucial.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=192)** By leveraging BERT's pre-trained language understanding, we can fine-tune it on a small dataset of product reviews to perform sentiment analysis.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=205)** This approach will maximize the utility of the limited data.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=210)** To do that, we're going to use the BertTokenizer, as we did before, to tokenize the data, and now we're going to use the TFBert for sequence classification, which is a type of auto-model that adds a layer on top of BERT to do classification.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=231)** Then, for example, we can tokenize a review, any review, compile a model, and we can fit it or just use it, and it's going to work.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=241)** This is the beauty of transfer learning.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=245)** Our third example involves detecting plant diseases from images using a scarce data set of plant leaf images.
>
> **[4:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=255)** MobileNet, a lightweight convolutional neural network, is well-suited for this task.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=262)** MobileNet, which was pre-trained on ImageNet, is optimized for mobile and embedded patient applications.
>
> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=271)** Its architecture balances accuracy and efficiency, making it ideal for scenarios with limited computational resources and data.
>
> **[4:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=283)** By adding a new classification layer to MobileNet and freezing it base layers as we did before, we'll adapt the model to identify those plant diseases using that limited set of labeled images.
>
> **[5:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=300)** Here again, we are going to use MobileNet, we are going to use it as a base model, then we grab its output.
>
> **[5:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=309)** We will do a Pooling just to grab more information out of the features.
>
> **[5:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=314)** We do a Dense layer, basic head, and then the predictions.
>
> **[5:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=319)** In this case, we have 10 possibilities of plant diseases, and that's it.
>
> **[5:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=324)** We create the model, we set the base_model as non-trainable, and that's it.
>
> **[5:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=330)** We can compile and fit.
>
> **[5:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=332)** And this will detect plant diseases.
>
> **[5:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=335)** This is the way that, for example, some apps work that you have to take a picture, and they will tell you which plant it is and what you should do with it.
>
> **[5:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=345)** In summary, choosing the right model for transfer learning involves evaluating the similarity between tasks, the pre-trained model capabilities, and your specific dataset constraints.
>
> **[5:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/choosing-models-for-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=359)** VGG for medical imaging, BERT for language tasks, and MobileNet for resource-efficient vision applications, demonstrate how transfer learning can be effectively applied across different domains.

#### Demo: Transfer learning with FLAN-T5
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-transfer-learning-with-flan-t5?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>

#### Evaluating transfer learning outcomes
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Now that we've seen transfer learning in action, let's focus on evaluating the outcomes of transfer learning, specifically, using metrics like ROUGE and BLEU.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=12)** These metrics are essential for assessing the quality of tasks, such as text summarization and machine translation, analogous to how accuracy's used in classification tasks.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=27)** Let's start by understanding ROUGE and BLEU.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=30)** Think of ROUGE as a measure of overlap between generated text and reference text, much like comparing how much two recipes share the same ingredients.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=43)** BLEU, on the other hand, measures how well the generated text matches the reference text, similar to comparing two completed dishes to see how closely they resemble each other in taste and presentation.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=60)** ROUGE stands for Recall-Oriented Understudy for Gisting Evaluation.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=66)** It's primarily used to evaluate the quality of summaries by measuring the overlap between the generated summary and a set of reference summaries.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=79)** Imagine comparing a new summary to a gold standard summary, checking how many of the key phrases and words overlap.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=88)** For example, consider two sentences.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=92)** The generated summary is "The cat sat on the mat."
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=98)** The reference summary is "The cat is sitting on the mat."
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=104)** To calculate ROUGE-1, that would mean unigram overlap, we would count the number of overlapping words and divide by the total number of words in the reference summary.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=119)** In this case, the overlapping words are the, cat, on, the, mat.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=126)** The only difference relies on "sat" versus "sitting."
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=131)** Therefore, ROUGE-1 would be 5/6, or 83%.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=137)** Such as ROUGE-1, there is ROUGE-2, ROUGE-3, and so on.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=142)** We normally present the first three and we consider those to be okay.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=148)** BLEU, on the other hand, stands for Bilingual Evaluation Understudy.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=154)** It measures how closely the generated text matches the reference text by comparing anangrams, that means sequences of n words.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=164)** BLEU is like a meticulous food critic, who not only checks if ingredients are correct, but also if they are combined in the right order and proportions.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=175)** As an example of a calculation of BLEU, let's consider the same generation, "The cat sat on the mat," and the same reference, "The cat is sitting on the mat."
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=186)** To calculate BLEU-1, we would count the number of matching unigrams and divide by the total number of unigrams in the generated text before it was in the reference one.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=200)** So now, the BLEU-1 would be five out of five, so it would be 100%.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=206)** You can think of BLEU as a precision count and ROUGE as a recall count, if you remember from classification tasks.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=216)** As a matter of fact, both ROUGE and BLEU are crucial in evaluating text generation tasks, similar to how accuracy's used in classification tasks.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=228)** While ROUGE focuses on recall, capturing how much of the reference summary is present in the generated summary, BLEU focuses on precision, assessing how well the generated text matches the reference in terms of exact phrases and their order.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=248)** It is important to mention that even though here we are talking about memorization, ROUGE and BLEU are both used as well in neural machine translation or question answering, or basically any text-to-text task.
>
> **[4:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=266)** Let's look at practical applications with some code examples using the Hugging Face library.
>
> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=272)** So here, first we're going to load metric, and we're going to load ROUGE just because we want to, and we're going to compare the generated summaries against reference summaries.
>
> **[4:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=284)** The same ones that we just said, "The cat sat on the mat," and "the cat is sitting on the mat."
>
> **[4:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=290)** To do that calculation, we just need to do ROUGE to compute.
>
> **[4:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=295)** We pass the predictions and the references and we print the results, and that's the code to run ROUGE.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=302)** I encourage you to take this code and now run it to see the results.
>
> **[5:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=308)** On the other hand, if we want to use BLEU, it's the same idea.
>
> **[5:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=313)** We just load the metric BLEU, and we then take the generated text, the reference text, and based on that we do bleu.compute.
>
> **[5:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=323)** Again, I encourage you to stop the video, try both metrics on code, and see how the actual framework presents them.
>
> **[5:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=333)** Understanding and utilizing ROUGE and BLEU metrics is essential for evaluating text generation tasks effectively.
>
> **[5:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/evaluating-transfer-learning-outcomes?u=76281980&t=346)** By comparing these metrics to accuracy and classification, we can better appreciate their role in assessing the quality of AI-generated text.

>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/solution-enhancing-translation-with-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=184)** We are going to get one batch from the test dataset, generate the output, and then we're going to get the reference and the hypothesis by decoding the actual reference, so the real value, and the output of the mode generation.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/solution-enhancing-translation-with-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=202)** We calculate the bleu.

>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/solution-enhancing-translation-with-transfer-learning?u=76281980&t=210)** So let's run this.

### 5. 4. PEFT Fine-Tuning with LoRA

#### Introduction to PEFT
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=0)** - We've talked about prompt engineering and transfer learning for fine-tuning.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=4)** Now, we are going to explore parameter-efficient fine-tuning or PEFT.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=9)** We'll explain what PEFT is, how it differs from traditional fine-tuning and transfer learning, and why it's especially valuable when we have little data.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=21)** To keep things engaging, we'll use our cooking analogy to illustrate these concepts.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=26)** Imagine you're a chef working with limited ingredients.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=31)** You need to create a gourmet dish without having access to a full pantry.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=36)** This is similar to the challenge faced in machine learning when data is little.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=44)** Traditional fine-tuning might require a lot of resources, akin to having a well-stocked kitchen.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=50)** PEFT, however, is like mastering the art of cooking with what little you have, optimizing each ingredient's use.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=59)** PEFT focuses on modifying a small subset of a model's parameters rather than the entire model.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=67)** This approach is highly efficient, making it possible to achieve significant improvements in performance without the need of extensive retraining.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=78)** Let's break down the differences.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=80)** In traditional fine-tuning, you adjust all the parameters of a pre-trained model to adapt it to a new task.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=87)** It's like reworking an entire recipe from scratch.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=91)** Transfer learning involves taking a pre-trained model, adding new layers or heads to it, similar to adding a new garnish or a sauce to a finished dish.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=103)** PEFT, on the other hand, involves adding small components called adapters.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=109)** Think of adapters as specialized tools or techniques that enhance the dish without altering the core recipe.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=119)** These adapters allow the model to learn new tasks efficiently using minimal additional data.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=127)** Adapters are lightweight modules inserted into a pre-trained model.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=133)** During training, only these adapters are updated while the rest of the model remains unchanged.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=140)** This method significantly reduces the computational resources required and makes the training process faster and more efficient.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=150)** For instance, if you're training a language model to understand legal documents, you could insert adapters that specialize in legal terminology and context.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=161)** These adapters are trained with your limited dataset, adapting the model to perform well on this specific task without needing to retrain the entire model.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=173)** Why is PEFT crucial when data is little?
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=176)** It's all about efficiency.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=178)** With PEFT, you can achieve high performance with fewer data points with less computational power.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=186)** This is particularly beneficial in scenarios where collecting large amounts of labeled data is impractical or too costly.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=195)** In summary, parameter-efficient fine-tuning or PEFT is a powerful technique that offers an efficient alternative to traditional fine-tuning and transfer learning, particularly when dealing with limited data.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=211)** By using adapters, PEFT optimizes the learning process, ensuring that even with little data, you can still achieve excellent results.
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-peft?u=76281980&t=223)** This makes PEFT an essential tool in the modern AI toolkit.

#### LoRA adapters
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Let's explore LoRa adapters, a powerful subset of parameter-efficient fine tuning, or PEFT, where we'll start with a high-level overview using our cooking analogy, and then we will dive deeper and deeper into the technical details.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=22)** Imagine you're a chef with a fantastic recipe.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=26)** You want to enhance your dish without overhauling the entire cooking process.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=33)** You bring a specialized tool like a microplane for zesting.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=39)** This tool makes a big impact with minimal effort.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=45)** In the world of machine learning, LoRa adapters play a similar role.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=51)** They provide a significant improvement without modifying the entire model.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=59)** LoRa stands for Low-Rank Adaptation.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=64)** These adapters are designed to fine-tune pre-trained models efficiently by focusing on a small subset of parameters.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=77)** They are particularly effective when you need to adapt a model to new tasks with limited data.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=86)** In this case, let's assume that we have three different tasks.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=91)** Instead of having three copies of a 13.5 gigabyte model, maybe fine-tuned or transfer learned, we're going to see a better strategy.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=108)** Technically, LoRa adapters are matrices that are inserted into the layers of a neural network.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=116)** Instead of updating the entire weight matrix, which is gigantic, during training, LoRa updates only this smaller low rank, therefore the name, matrices.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=131)** This approach significantly reduces the number of parameters that needs to be trained.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=138)** Let's go a bit deeper.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=140)** In a typical neural network layer, weights are represented by a large matrix.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=147)** During fine tuning, this matrix is adjusted to improve model performance.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=153)** However, this process can be computationally expensive and require lots of data.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=161)** Let's assume in our example of LoRa, that n, that means the size of the matrix, is 512, which is quite conservative.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=172)** And let's assume for the extreme case that we are going to take r, that means the rank of the LoRa adapter, as one.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=182)** That means that if we take the amount of parameters that we need to fine-tune in LoRa, would be only 500 times one times, well, the floating point 32 precision, times two, which is 32,000 parameters instead of the 512 squared parameters, which is more than 2 million.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=209)** This is almost 20 times less parameters to tune.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=214)** So you can see that it is gigantic effect.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=218)** In LoRa, as we said, these two matrices, A and B, are used such that we can decompose the matrix W into the matrix multiplication of A and B, A being sample from a normal distribution.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=240)** And by this then the trick is that we can change those little weights and make a huge, huge change.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=248)** If this was very, very technical, don't worry about it, because you don't really need to know the mathematics behind LoRa to understand exactly how to implement it.
>
> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=261)** Okay, so don't worry.
>
> **[4:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=264)** As we said, the main thing to keep in mind is that now the new weights that we are going to do our training will be some frozen pre-trained weights, W, plus the matrix multiplication of A and B, which are much, much smaller, okay?
>
> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=285)** Again, don't worry about the math if you are not familiar with linear algebra.
>
> **[4:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=290)** Just take the important concept.
>
> **[4:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=292)** We have two matrices, A and B.
>
> **[4:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=295)** They will be small.
>
> **[4:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=297)** The amount of parameters to tune will be much, much less, and we'll have the same level of efficiency.
>
> **[5:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=305)** This method is not only computationally efficient, but also requires much less data.
>
> **[5:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=313)** Because A and B are low rank matrices, the number of parameters to update is drastically reduced, making the training process faster and less resource intensive.
>
> **[5:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=327)** This is particularly important in your case if you do not have access to A100 or L4 GPUs.
>
> **[5:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=336)** Think of it like using a set of specialized tools in cooking.
>
> **[5:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=342)** Each tool makes a small but significant enhancement to the dish without changing the core recipe.
>
> **[5:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=350)** Similarly, LoRa adapters make precise adjustments to the model, enhancing its performance without a complete retraining.
>
> **[6:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=361)** If this level of detail feels a bit too mathematical or deep, that's perfectly okay.
>
> **[6:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=368)** If I want you to leave with one message, it's that LoRa adapters provide a highly efficient way to fine-tune models, especially when data is scarce and computational resources are limited.
>
> **[6:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=388)** To summarize, LoRa adapters are a subset of PEFT that use low-rank matrices to fine-tune models efficiently.
>
> **[6:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=399)** By updating only a small number of parameters, they offer significant performance improvements with minimal computational cost.
>
> **[6:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-adapters?u=76281980&t=409)** This makes them an invaluable tool for adapting pre-trained models to new tasks.
