#### LoRA in depth: Technical analysis
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Let's dive deeper into the technical aspects of how to implement LoRA adapters.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=7)** We'll discuss challenges like overfitting versus modern generalizability, rank selection, and parameter tuning.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=17)** And as always, we'll use our cooking analogy to keep things simple and relatable.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=24)** Imagine you are a chef trying to perfect a new dish.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=28)** You might add a lot of different spices to make it taste great, but there's this risk of overdoing it, making the dish too complex or overpowering.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=40)** Similarly, when implementing LoRa, one of the key challenges is balancing the model's performance to avoid overfitting while ensuring it generalizes well to new data.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=54)** Overfitting occurs when a model learns the training data too well, capturing noise and details that don't generalize to new unseen data.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=66)** It's like a dish that's tailored to exact tastes of a few people, but doesn't appeal to a broader audience.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=78)** Generalizability, on the other hand, is about making sure the model performs well on new data, similar to creating a dish that pleases a wide range of palates.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=92)** In the context of LoRa, this means fine-tuning the low-rank matrices in a way that improves performance without losing the model's ability to handle varied inputs.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=106)** Next, let's talk about rank selection.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=111)** Choosing the right rank for your LoRA adapters is crucial.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=115)** It's like choosing the right tool in the kitchen.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=119)** Using a Microplane for zesting is perfect, but using it for grating cheese would be inefficient.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=128)** Similarly, the rank determines how many parameters are introduced and tuned.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=135)** A lower rank means fewer parameters, which can help prevent overfitting, but might limit the model's capacity to learn complex patterns.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=148)** Conversely, a higher rank introduces more parameters, enhancing learning capacity, but increasing the risk of overfitting.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=160)** A practical advice for rank selection would include starting with a lower rank and gradually increase it while monitoring the model's performance and validation data.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=173)** This approach helps finding that balance between under and overfitting.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=180)** Parameter tuning in LoRa is like seasoning a dish.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=184)** You need to find the right amount of each ingredient to make the dish perfect.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=190)** This involves adjusting the learning rate, batch size, and the number of epoch to optimize model training.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=198)** The learning rate controls how much the model's parameters are adjusted during training.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=205)** A rate too high can cause the model to converge too quickly to a suboptimal solution, like adding too much salt at once.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=215)** A rate that's too low can make training very slow, akin to seasoning too cautiously.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=224)** The batch size and the number of epochs are also crucial.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=228)** A large batch size can stabilize training, but requires much more memory, similar to preparing a large batch of food.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=240)** The number of epochs or complete passes through the training data needs to be enough to ensure the model learns, but not so much that it overfits.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=253)** A practical advice for parameter tuning includes starting with common default values, and using techniques like cross-validation to iteratively find the best settings.
>
> **[4:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=266)** Monitoring validation loss and performance metrics helps guide these adjustments.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=273)** In summary, implementing LoRA adapters involves careful consideration of overfitting versus generalizability, selecting the appropriate rank and fine-tuning parameters.
>
> **[4:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=286)** By balancing these aspects, you can enhance your model performance effectively.
>
> **[4:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/lora-in-depth-technical-analysis?u=76281980&t=292)** Remember, just like in cooking, the key is to adjust, taste, and then retest frequently to achieve the best results.

>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=231)** Perfect. So how do we implement LoRA?
>
> **[3:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=235)** We need to create a Keras layer and then the idea will be to replace a specific type of layer in our model with this layer.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=245)** To make it easy for this first approach, you are going to just replace the dense layers, okay?
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=253)** So every time you see a dense layer in the model, you're going to replace it with a LoRA layer.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=259)** So in the init, we need the rank.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=262)** Remember that will determine the amount of parameters of LoRA.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=265)** That will also determine the size of the matrices and the actual layer, which I call here dense.
>
> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=272)** This means the actual dense layer that comes.
>
> **[4:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=275)** Why I need it, because I need its output to do the output plus A times B, remember, and I also need it to set it as non trainable.
>
> **[4:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=288)** On the building of the layer, the build method is what is being called when we in instantiate that layer and it's appended to the model on the compiling of the computational graph.
>
> **[5:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=300)** We'll create two matrices, A and B, the same as we did in the slides where we use the add weight method from Keras.
>
> **[5:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=310)** The shape it's important, the A comes first.
>
> **[5:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=314)** It's A times B, so from matrix multiplication, the second dimension of the first matrix needs to be equal to the first dimension of the second matrix.
>
> **[5:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=327)** That's why it says self rank on both place as we want the final dimension to be exactly equal to the original layer.
>
> **[5:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=339)** The first dimension of the first matrix and the last dimension of the second matrix need to match the one of the dense layers.
>
> **[5:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=349)** We will initialize them as random normal matrices, but remember we are going to train them.
>
> **[5:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=357)** Finally, when we call this layer, we're going to first call the dense layers of the normal original output we would get.
>
> **[6:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=366)** Then we do the actual A times B and apply it on the inputs, which we do with the matrix multiplication 2 times.
>
> **[6:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=375)** That will be the LoRA output.
>
> **[6:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=377)** We set the dense layer as non trainable, and finally we return the addition of the 2.
>
> **[6:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=384)** This is the implementation of a LoRA layer. Okay?
>
> **[6:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=389)** Remember this.
>
> **[6:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=392)** Now if we see our model, the issue with Hugging Face models is that they are normally packed.
>
> **[6:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-lora-fine-tuning-on-flan-t5?u=76281980&t=399)** What I mean with this is that, for example, if you see the encoder or decoder, they are a specific layer.

> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=124)** Now that we have our layer, we will integrate this LoRA adapter into the model's existing layer.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=133)** Okay?
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=134)** For simplicity, we'll add LoRA to the dense layer.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=138)** Just to make it very simple.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=141)** To do that, we need to create a new layer class, LoRA dense layer, that will take the adapter, LoRA adapter.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=150)** And in the call method, and this is the important thing, we will take the original output, we'll take the LoRA output, and then we're going to add them up.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=161)** This is exactly a LoRA part.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=164)** That operation, original output plus LoRA output, is our W + AB I told you about.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=172)** After doing that, what we would need to do is we need to replace the dense layers of the model with these new LoRA dense layers that know how to do LoRA.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=190)** And that's what we do in this place.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=194)** In this example, we replace the existing dense layers with our new LoRA dense layer, which therefore integrates the LoRA adapters.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=205)** This allows us to fine tune only a subset of parameters.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=211)** Finally, we compile and train the model.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=216)** We'll use a sample dataset for demonstration purposes.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=221)** Here we will load and process the WMT16 English German dataset.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=229)** We'll compile the model with the Adam Optimizer and start the training process.
>
> **[3:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=235)** So we'll load that dataset from German to English.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=239)** We'll use the data collator just to ensure that all the remaining parts of batches are of the correct size.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=249)** And now we need to create our dataset.
>
> **[4:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=252)** To create a dataset, what we need to do, as always, is to tokenize the data.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=257)** So we're going to map the data set, both the training and the test set, with the Lambda that will apply the tokenizer to the correct translation to create the labels.
>
> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=271)** After we do all of that and we have our data ready, what we have to do is just compile the model with Adam Optimizer as we normally do, and we fit the model.
>
> **[4:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=286)** And that will just work.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/implementing-lora-in-llms?u=76281980&t=289)** This way, we have effectively implemented LoRA by replacing each of the dense layers of the Flan T5 Large model into LoRA layers.

> **[4:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/solution-finetuning-the-summarization-model?u=76281980&t=298)** For that, we're going to calculate the BLEU score for each of the inputs of the batch, and then we're going to return an average BLEU score.
>
> **[5:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/solution-finetuning-the-summarization-model?u=76281980&t=305)** So we'll run that.
>
> **[5:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/solution-finetuning-the-summarization-model?u=76281980&t=308)** It shouldn't take more than a minute or two, and we'll get an average BLEU score.
>
> **[5:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/solution-finetuning-the-summarization-model?u=76281980&t=314)** Perfect, it took about 39 seconds, and in our case you can see that our BLEU score was 0.03, which is really good.
>
> **[5:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/solution-finetuning-the-summarization-model?u=76281980&t=324)** Perfect.
>
> **[5:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/solution-finetuning-the-summarization-model?u=76281980&t=326)** If you wanted better values, you know you can use a larger model, more data, or even here, it will take a little longer, but you can set the max length of the generated answer, that means the summary, maybe to 512 or 1,024, so the model has more room to create the summary.
>
> **[5:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/solution-finetuning-the-summarization-model?u=76281980&t=346)** Remember that after all, that's how BLEU works.
>
> **[5:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/solution-finetuning-the-summarization-model?u=76281980&t=350)** Overall, we got a summarization model to apply to our chatbot.

> **[9:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/fine-tuning-for-llms-from-beginner-to-advanced/demo-integrating-everything-into-our-solution?u=76281980&t=572)** And to leverage an LLM in a chatbot or any application is always the same process, tokenizer model.generate and decode, as we have learned during the whole course.

>
